<p><b>José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</b> (<small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[xoseˈlwis roˈðɾiɣeθ θapaˈteɾo]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-Jos%C3%A9_Lu%C3%ADs_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero.oga" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7b/Es-Jos%C3%A9_Lu%C3%ADs_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero.oga" class="internal" title="Es-José Luís Rodríguez Zapatero.oga">listen</a></span></span>)</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> born 4 August 1960) is a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> politician and member of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a> (PSOE). He was the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister of Spain</a> being elected for two terms, in the <a href="/wiki/2004_Spanish_legislative_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Spanish legislative election">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Spanish_legislative_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Spanish legislative election">2008</a> general elections.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> On 2 April 2011 he announced he would not stand for re-election in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Spanish_general_election" title="2011 Spanish general election">2011 general election</a> and left office on 21 December 2011.
</p><p>Among the main actions taken by the Zapatero administration were <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq#2004_withdrawals" title="Multi-National Force – Iraq">the withdrawal of Spanish troops from the Iraq war</a>, the increase of Spanish troops in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>; the idea of an <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Civilizations" title="Alliance of Civilizations">Alliance of Civilizations</a>; the legalisation of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain" title="Same-sex marriage in Spain">same-sex marriage in Spain</a>; reform of abortion law; a  <a href="/wiki/ETA%27s_2006_%22permanent_ceasefire%22" class="mw-redirect" title="ETA&#39;s 2006 &quot;permanent ceasefire&quot;">peace negotiation</a> attempt with <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a>;  increase of <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">tobacco</a> restrictions; and the reform of various <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous community">autonomous statutes</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Statute of Catalonia">Statute of Catalonia</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_background">Family background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Family background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero was born in <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, Castile and León, to Juan Rodríguez y García-Lozano (born 1928), a lawyer, and María de la Purificación Zapatero Valero (<a href="/wiki/Tordehumos" title="Tordehumos">Tordehumos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valladolid_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Valladolid (province)">Valladolid</a>, 1927 – <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, 30 October 2000). He grew up in <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Spain" title="León, Spain">León</a>, where his family originated.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His paternal grandfather, Juan Rodríguez y Lozano (28 July 1893 – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Puente_Castro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puente Castro (page does not exist)">Puente Castro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (province)">León</a>, 18 August 1936), was a <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Captain_(land_and_air)" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain (land and air)">captain</a>, executed by Francisco Franco's National army a month into the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, for refusing to fight with them.<sup id="cite_ref-cidob_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cidob-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> His whereabouts were revealed by fascists in Valladolid.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His maternal grandfather, Faustino Valentín Zapatero Ballesteros (<a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, 14 February 1899 – 1978), was a <a href="/wiki/Paediatrics" class="mw-redirect" title="Paediatrics">paediatrician</a> and middle class liberal. His maternal grandmother María de la Natividad Valero y Asensio (<a href="/wiki/Zamora,_Spain" title="Zamora, Spain">Zamora</a>, 9 December 1902 – Valladolid, 28 June 2006) was a conservative and died at age 103.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Zapatero was born in Valladolid not only because of his mother's attachment to her family, who lived there, but also because of the medical profession of her father.
</p><p>Zapatero has said that, as a youngster, "as I remember it, I used to participate in late night conversations with my father and brother about politics, law or literature". However, he did not get along very well with his father at times. Sources say that his father refused to let him work or take any part in his law firm,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and this scarred him for life.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He says that his family taught him to be tolerant, thoughtful, prudent and austere.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The memory of Republican Captain Rodríguez y Lozano was also kept alive by his last <a href="/wiki/Will_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Will (law)">will</a>, handwritten 24 hours before facing the firing squad, and which can be considered a final declaration of principles. The will comprised six parts, the first three bestowing his possessions on his heirs; the fourth, in which he asked for a civil burial and, the fifth, in which he requested his family to forgive those who had tried and executed him and proclaiming his belief in the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Being" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Being">Supreme Being</a>. In the sixth, Zapatero's grandfather asked his family to clear his name in the future as his creed consisted only in his "love for peace, for good and for improving the living conditions of the lower classes".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to an Israeli newspaper, <a href="/wiki/Maariv_(newspaper)" title="Maariv (newspaper)">Maariv</a>, by Zapatero's own statement: "My family, named Zapatero, is of Jewish descent", probably from a family of <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">Marranos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He is an agnostic.<sup id="cite_ref-agnostic_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agnostic-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Studies_and_teaching">Studies and teaching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Studies and teaching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He studied Law at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="University of León">University of León</a>, graduating in 1982. His performance as a student was above average before his pre-University year. According to his brother Juan: "He didn't study much but it made no difference, he continued successfully".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After graduating, Zapatero worked as a teaching assistant in constitutional law at the University of León until 1986 (he continued working some hours a week without pay until 1991). It was subsequently found that he had been appointed by his department without the usual selection process involving interviews and competitive examinations, which if true, constitutes a case of political favouritism.<sup id="cite_ref-cidob_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cidob-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He has declared that the only activity that attracts him besides politics is teaching or, at most, academic research.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rodríguez Zapatero met <a href="/wiki/Sonsoles_Espinosa" title="Sonsoles Espinosa">Sonsoles Espinosa</a> in León in 1981. They married on 27 January 1990 and have two daughters named Laura (b. 1993) and Alba (b. 1995).
</p><p>Having received successive deferments because of his conditions as a university student and a teaching assistant, Zapatero did not do the compulsory military service. As an <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> he was finally exempted.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entering_politics">Entering politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Entering politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:185px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg/183px-Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg" decoding="async" width="183" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg/275px-Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg/366px-Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1933" data-file-height="1588" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Congresodiputados_10_05_88.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Zapatero having a break during a parliamentary session with some fellow Socialist MPs in 1988.</div></div></div>
<p>Zapatero attended his first political rally, organized by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a> (PSOE) in <a href="/wiki/Gij%C3%B3n" title="Gijón">Gijón</a> in 1976. Some political parties had been legal since 21 July 1976, but the PSOE was not legalized until February 1977. The speech of <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Felipe González">Felipe González</a>, the PSOE leader and future <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister of Spain</a>, who took part in the rally, exerted an important influence on Zapatero. He said, among other things, that "the Socialists' goal was the seizure of power by the working class to transform the ownership of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>" and that "the PSOE was a revolutionary party but not <i>revolutionarist</i> or <i>aventurist</i> [...], as it defended the use of elections to come to power".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero and his family had been traditionally attracted to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Spain_(main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of Spain (main)">Communist Party</a> as it was the only party really organized before <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>'s death in 1975.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> But, after the famous political rally in Gijón, they, and especially Zapatero, started to believe that the Socialist Party was the most probable future for the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Political_left" class="mw-redirect" title="Political left">left</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p111_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p111-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> At that time the Socialist Party was rebuilding its infrastructure in the province of León after having been outlawed following the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1977, the year of the first democratic elections after Franco's death, Zapatero supported both the Communist and Socialist parties. He pasted posters of both parties.<sup id="cite_ref-p111_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p111-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He eventually joined the PSOE on 23 February 1979. The impression Felipe González had caused on him in 1976 played a fundamental role in his decision to join the party. In 1979, during the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Congreso_Extraordinario_del_PSOE_(1979)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Congreso Extraordinario del PSOE (1979) (page does not exist)">Congreso Extraordinario del PSOE (1979)</a>, the PSOE had renounced <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> as its ideological base. He said nothing about joining the party at home, because he was afraid his parents would discourage him, considering him too young to join a political party.
</p><p>In 1982, Zapatero became head of the socialist youth organization in the province of <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (province)">León</a>. In July 1982, he met Felipe González at the summer school "Jaime Vera" and suggested that he make a "left turn" in the PSOE political program for the General Election of October 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> González answered advising him to abandon his conservative (traditional for PSOE [leftist]) viewpoint.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1986, he was elected to represent the province of León in the <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Cortes</a> (Parliament), becoming its youngest member after the election held on 20 June. He was number two on the PSOE list for <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(Spanish_Congress_Electoral_District)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (Spanish Congress Electoral District)">León</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In the following elections (those held in 1989, 1993, 1996 and 2000) he was number one on the list. In the elections of 2004 he ran for <a href="/wiki/Madrid_(Spanish_Congress_Electoral_District)" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid (Spanish Congress Electoral District)">Madrid</a> as number one.
</p><p>Zapatero defined himself as a "left-wing conservative" at the time. He explained that he meant that, for sentimental reasons linked to his family, he came from the left that lost the Spanish Civil War and that what had happened between 1936–1939 (the duration of the war) and 1939–1975 (<a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Franco</a>'s regime) had a very important significance for him. He further explained that the Spanish left needed to modernize and that "we are finding it difficult to accept the need for the Socialist Party to change many of its ideological parameters and overcome our own conservatism".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1988 he became Secretary General in León after a complex internal fight for power that ended a long period of division. In fact, before the provincial conference held that year, <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Rubial" title="Ramón Rubial">Ramón Rubial</a>, then national president of the PSOE, had asked the party in León to foster unity. Zapatero was elected as Secretary General at that conference, leading to a period of stability.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1980s and 1990s, the PSOE consisted of two factions: the <i>Guerristas</i> (supporters of <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Guerra" title="Alfonso Guerra">Alfonso Guerra</a>, former vice-president under Felipe González) and the reformers (led by Felipe González). The first group had a stronger left-wing ideology whereas the second was more pragmatic. The division became wider after the General Election of 1993, the last election won by the PSOE before <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a>'s victory in 1996, when the bad results exacerbated the internal conflicts. Zapatero never formally joined either of those two groups.
</p><p>In 1993, the Socialist Federation of León (FSL – Federación Socialista de León) suffered an important scandal. Some towns experienced unusually sharp increases in PSOE membership in a very short period of time. When some of the supposed new members were questioned by the press, they stated that they were unaware of their membership and that they did not live in the places where they were being registered by the party. It seems that some opponents of Zapatero in León, perhaps with the support of powerful <i>Guerristas</i> at the top of the Spanish Socialist Party wanted to increase their influence within it by increasing the number of members in the towns of León favorable to them. Their main aim would have been to take control of the Regional Socialist Section of <a href="/wiki/Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Castilla y León">Castilla y León</a> in the conference to be held in 1994. Zapatero's support for the then Regional Secretary General, Jesús Quijano transformed him into the enemy of the <i>Guerristas</i> in the region as the FSL is the most important Provincial Section.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 1994 two papers, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El País">El País</a></i> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diario_de_Le%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Diario de León (page does not exist)">Diario de León</a></i>, published several articles that suggested irregularities in his appointment as a teaching assistant by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="University of León">University of León</a> and in his keeping the job until 1991. The suspicions of political favoritism were due to his having been directly appointed without a prior selection process open to other candidates. On 20 May 1994, he held a press conference where he rejected these accusations. Zapatero attributed to "ignorance" or "bad faith" the content of the articles and linked them to the internal fight for the job of Secretary General of the Regional Chapter.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, three regional conferences were held: All of them were finally won by Zapatero or his supporters.
</p><p>The National Conference (held after most of the representatives elected in the first León Conference were Zapatero's supporters) was won by the <i>reformers</i>, at that time strongly opposed to the <i>Guerristas</i>. That was positive for Zapatero as the list of bogus party members was revised again. Their number grew from 577 to almost 900.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero was finally reelected secretary general with 68% of the ballots in the 7th Regional Conference held in July 1994, following the removal of the false memberships.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1995, new regional and local elections were held. The results were bad for the PSOE in León as they lost four seats in the mayoralty of León and two seats in the regional parliament of Castilla-León. The results were influenced by the bad economic situation and the cases of corruption assailing the party. Zapatero had personally directed the electoral campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1996, after the General Election, Zapatero kept his seat at the Congress of Deputies. The following year, Zapatero was again elected Secretary General of León and after the national conference held by the party that year he entered the National Executive (the party's governing body).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Association of Parliamentary Journalists awarded to Zapatero the "Diputado Revelación" prize (something like <i>Most promising MP of the year</i>) in December 1999 for his activities as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">Congress of Deputies</a>. From 1996 until 2000, his most conspicuous contributions as an MP were his vigorous opposition to the electrical protocol proposed by the government (initially negative for the important coal sector of León), being the PSOE spokesman in the Commission of Public Administration<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and probably his most important success as an MP: the passing of an amendment to the national budget of 2000 in November 1999 that increased the pensions of the non-professional soldiers who fought for the Republic during the Spanish Civil War of 1936–1939. They were made equal to those of the professional military. The initiative was defended by him in the name of the Parliamentary Socialist Group, proponent of the amendment.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appointment_as_Secretary_General_of_the_Socialist_Party">Appointment as Secretary General of the Socialist Party</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Appointment as Secretary General of the Socialist Party">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 12 March 2000, the PSOE had lost its second successive election to José María Aznar's <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party</a>. Zapatero held his seat, but the Socialist Party obtained only 125 seats, 16 fewer than in 1996. The defeat was especially bitter as the People's Party unexpectedly obtained an absolute majority for the first time and the socialist result was worse than in the previous election. Almunia announced his resignation on the very day the General Election took place.
</p><p>Zapatero decided to run for the leadership of the Socialist Party in its 35th Conference to be held in June that year. Together with other socialist members, he founded a new faction within the party called <i>Nueva Vía</i> (New Way) in April 2000, to serve him as a platform to become Secretary General. The name of <i>Nueva Vía</i> is a mix of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Third_Way_(centrism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Way (centrism)">Third Way</a></i> (<i>tercera vía</i> in Spanish) and <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Gerhard Schröder">Gerhard Schröder</a>'s <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neue_Mitte&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Neue Mitte (page does not exist)">Neue Mitte</a></i> (<i>new center</i> or <i>nuevo centro</i> in Spanish).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 June 2000 Zapatero officially announced his intention to run for the federal Secretaryship General at an Extraordinary Conference of the Socialist Party of León.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In his speech, he stated what can be considered his declaration of principles:<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>To build a society that would accept all foreigners notwithstanding their color or cultural background.</li>
<li>To give priority to education and to create good jobs for youngsters.</li>
<li>To provide parents with more time to spend with their children and in taking care of their elders.</li>
<li>To promote culture and its creators, making it possible for them to grab the spotlight from those aiming only at economic interests.</li>
<li>To convert Spain into a country admired for helping those with more needs.</li>
<li>To force the government to help those with initiative and enterprising qualities.</li>
<li>To foster democracy, to lend distinction to politics and to promote values over temporary interests.</li></ol>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pasqual_Maragall" title="Pasqual Maragall">Pasqual Maragall</a> was the only regional leader of the Socialist Party who officially supported him before the Conference was held. José Borrell also decided to support him.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero ran against three other opponents (<a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bono" class="mw-redirect" title="José Bono">José Bono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosa_D%C3%ADez" title="Rosa Díez">Rosa Díez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matilde_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Matilde Fernández">Matilde Fernández</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Matilde Fernández was the candidate of the <i>guerristas</i> while José Bono was the candidate of the <i>reformers</i>. Rosa Díez is a Basque politician who was a kind of intermediate option.
</p><p>Zapatero was a <i>dark horse</i> who had against him his inexperience and in favour his image of reform and being the only MP among the candidates. (All the Spanish opposition leaders had been MPs before winning the elections. A very important factor in Spanish politics where electoral campaigns last for only 15 days and to be widely known long before they begin is essential.) Bono was deeply disliked by the <i>guerristas</i>, who also favoured Zapatero.
</p><p>Zapatero finally won by a relatively small margin (he obtained 414 votes out of 995 and José Bono obtained 405) on 22 July 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The margin was relatively small because Bono had no likelihood of winning since the supporters of the other two candidates preferred Zapatero as their second choice. Zapatero accepted the cancellation of a run-off between himself and Bono because he was sure of his victory after only one ballot and he apparently did not want to humiliate his adversary.
</p><p>After being elected Secretary General, he was congratulated by <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Jospin" title="Lionel Jospin">Lionel Jospin</a> (then the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_France" title="Prime Minister of France">Prime Minister of France</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Gerhard Schröder">Gerhard Schröder</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic)">Chancellor of Germany</a>) and José María Aznar.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He moved to <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> with his family that year. As a Congressman he had lived from Monday to Thursday in Madrid and the rest of the time in León.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_leader">Opposition leader</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Opposition leader">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This was the period when Zapatero was appointed as Secretary General  of the PSOE in 2000 until he became <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister of Spain</a> on 14 March 2004.
</p><p>Zapatero has always claimed to base his political activity on his love of dialogue. When he was an opposition leader, he liked to contrast his behaviour with the "arrogant", "<a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a>" approach of the People's Party and, especially, that of its leader José María Aznar.
</p><p>As a result, after being appointed Secretary General, he coined the term <i>Calm Opposition</i> (<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Oposición Tranquila</i>) to refer to his opposition strategy. The <i>Calm Opposition</i> was supposedly based on an "open to dialogue", "soft", "constructive" attitude (<i>talante constructivo</i>, coined as <i>talante</i>) aimed not at damaging the government but at achieving the "best" for the people. (Zapatero has insisted on this point so many times that the term <i>talante</i> has become very popular in Spain.) Because of this supposed tactic, Zapatero received nicknames like <i><a href="/wiki/Bambi" title="Bambi">Bambi</a></i> or <i>Sosoman</i> (where <i>Soso</i>, meaning "dull, insipid, bore", replaces <i>Super</i> in <i><a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a></i>), especially in the first months after being appointed General Secretary.
</p><p>After his election to the leadership of the PSOE, Zapatero spoke about the influence of the political philosophy of <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">civic republicanism</a> on him in general, and in particular the ideas of republican political philosopher <a href="/wiki/Philip_Pettit" title="Philip Pettit">Philip Pettit</a>. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)">El Mundo</a></i>, Zapatero linked civic republicanism's focus on <a href="/wiki/Civic_virtue" title="Civic virtue">civic virtue</a> to tolerance of individual autonomy and expanding political participation.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During Zapatero's years as an opposition leader (and later as Prime Minister), the tension between left-wing and right-wing supporters increased and, according to some opinions, a real radicalization of the society took (and is taking) place<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Zapatero's supporters blame his opponents for that and the People's Party blames him stating facts such as the increase in the acts of violence committed against them, especially in the months before and during the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Iraq">war in Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> As a result, a new term has become popular: <i>guerracivilismo</i><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> (made up of a combination of the Spanish for Civil War and the <i>-ismo</i> <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a>, equivalent to the English "-ism"), which would refer to the growing enmity of right and left-wing factions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_and_2001">2000 and 2001</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000 and 2001">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Zapatero's criticisms of the government were very active from the beginning, blaming the government for its inability to control the rise in the price of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> and asking for a reduction in the corresponding taxes.
</p><p>In 2000, the British <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear submarine</a> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Tireless_(S88)" title="HMS Tireless (S88)">HMS&#160;<i>Tireless</i></a> arrived at <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> harbour to have its <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> repaired. Aznar affirmed that there was no risk for the population but Zapatero criticized him for his inability to force the British government to take the submarine to another harbour. After almost one year, the <i>Tireless</i> was repaired and left Gibraltar without having caused any known problems.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another point of friction came from the scheme to transfer water from the River Ebro to other areas, especially the irrigated areas in the South East of Spain, one of the richest agricultural regions in the world. The scheme had received support from, among others, 80% of the affected farmers and the Socialist regional governments of regions such as <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a>, Andalusia or <a href="/wiki/Castilla-La_Mancha" class="mw-redirect" title="Castilla-La Mancha">Castilla-La Mancha</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Some Socialist politicians also supported it when they were members of the former Socialist government back in the 90s (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Borrell" class="mw-redirect" title="José Borrell">José Borrell</a>, the current leader of the European Spanish Socialist Group and former president of the European Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The scheme was mainly opposed by Zapatero, environmentalist groups, the Socialist regional government of <a href="/wiki/Aragon,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Aragon, Spain">Aragon</a> and some of the citizens of the areas from which water was to be transferred. The main criticisms of the scheme were the supposed damage to the environment and an argued real lack of sufficient water for all of the affected parties (the proponents of the scheme answered back that there was no risk of a serious environmental damage and that in 2003, 14 times more water reached the sea than what was needed annually).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The scheme, finally approved by the Government, was canceled by Zapatero soon after becoming Prime Minister.
</p><p>Zapatero was the main proponent of the "Pacto de las Libertades contra el Terrorismo" ("Anti Terrorist Freedom pact) which was signed on 8 December 2000.
</p><p>At the end of the year, the <a href="/wiki/Bovine_spongiform_encephalopathy" title="Bovine spongiform encephalopathy">Mad Cow disease</a> came back into the spotlight after its outbreak in 1996. Zapatero repeatedly criticized the Government's management of the crisis arguing that it was out of control.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> As of March 2005, the disease had caused dozens of deaths all over Europe, though none in Spain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2001 one of the biggest points of friction between the government and the opposition were the proposed reforms affecting the education system. The People's Party first introduced the so-called LOU, a law to change the university system, and later the LOCE (<i>Organic Act for Education Quality</i>), which affected secondary education. Zapatero strongly opposed both. The People's Party used its absolute majority in the <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Cortes</a> to pass its reforms.
</p><p>A regional election was held in the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a> on 13 May 2001. The socialists received 17.8% of the vote (against 17.6% in the previous 1998 elections) but lost one seat. Both, the Socialist Party and the People's Party had formed an alliance against the then ruling nationalist Basque political movements but the latter won again. The results were considered a failure.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicol%C3%A1s_Redondo_Terreros&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nicolás Redondo Terreros (page does not exist)">Nicolás Redondo Terreros</a>, the Basque Socialist leader during the election who was strongly opposed to Basque nationalism and to <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a>, resigned after some internal clashes, resigning his seat in the Basque parliament and in the Federal Executive. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Patxi_L%C3%B3pez" title="Patxi López">Patxi López</a>, elected on 24 March 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> López had actively supported Zapatero during his campaign to become Secretary General. [OCAM p.&#160;257]
</p><p>On 21 October 2001 a new regional election took place, this time in <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>. The People's Party, led in Galicia by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Fraga_Iribarne" class="mw-redirect" title="Manuel Fraga Iribarne">Manuel Fraga Iribarne</a>, obtained a new absolute majority. The Socialist party increased its number of seats from 15 to 17, but, after several years of opposition the results were also considered bad.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> These two negative results seemed to confirm that Zapatero's approach was not working.
</p><p>On 19 December 2001 Zapatero travelled to <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, after the Moroccan government expelled the Spanish ambassador <a href="/wiki/Sine_die" class="mw-redirect" title="Sine die">sine die</a>. <a href="/wiki/Javier_Arenas_(Spanish_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Javier Arenas (Spanish politician)">Javier Arenas</a>, then secretary general of the People's Party, accused him of not being loyal to Spanish interests. Zapatero denied it and claimed that one of his purposes was to help solve the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_2002_to_2003">From 2002 to 2003</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: From 2002 to 2003">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, Zapatero was chosen as the Socialist candidate for the next general election.
</p><p>In 2002, the People's Party Government decided to reform the system of <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_benefits" title="Unemployment benefits">unemployment benefits</a>, as it thought that there were too many workers who being able to find a job preferred to continue receiving public money. This led to a redefinition of those who were eligible for unemployment benefits. Left-wing parties and trade unions considered that redefinition an unacceptable reduction of rights. Zapatero became the political leader of the opposition against the reform (dubbed the <i>Decretazo</i>, because it was passed using a decree-law), which served him as his first important clash with Aznar's government.
</p><p>A General Strike was announced for 20 June 2002 (the first since Aznar won the election in 1996). Although, according to official data (including the electrical power consumption and the number of working days calculated by the Social Security), the turnout was lower than 15%, the lowest since the restoration of democracy, neither the unions nor Zapatero believed the data and considered the strike a resounding success,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> with more than "10 million" workers having followed the strike. Whatever the result, both the People's Party government and the trade unions signed an agreement that satisfied both parties in November.
</p><p>In May 2002, Felipe González declared in reference to the change in the Socialist Party that "My state of mind tells me that a change has taken place, that perhaps a second Suresnes<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> has happened, but it has yet to be proved that a new project with content and ideas really exists", thus doubting Zapatero's leadership. That declaration was expressed in a public event also attended by Zapatero, who calmly expressed his disagreement. González ended his intervention by remembering that his candidate for Secretary General was <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bono" class="mw-redirect" title="José Bono">José Bono</a>, not Zapatero. González backtracked the next day, declaring that either his words had been incorrectly construed or he had expressed his ideas erroneously. José Bono himself confirmed his total support for Zapatero.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The incident seemed to confirm that Zapatero's strategy was not working.
</p><p>On 22 October 2002 Zapatero spoke in the name of the Socialist Party during the debate about the National Budget. Initially, <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Sevilla" title="Jordi Sevilla">Jordi Sevilla</a> was to have been the Socialist spokesman but, at the last moment, he was replaced in a surprise move. When Jordi Sevilla, after being called by the speaker, had already descended to the floor of the Congress of Deputies, Zapatero said to him "let me do it" and climbed to the orator platform. José María Aznar and other members of the People's Party had previously criticized him for not representing his party in the debate, suggesting a lack of the necessary political skills. Although the People's Party considered his action too theatrical, it seems it had quite a positive effect on his supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2002, the oil tanker <i><a href="/wiki/Prestige_oil_spill" title="Prestige oil spill">Prestige</a></i> suffered an accident in international waters<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> causing a grave oil slick which mainly affected Galicia, but also, to a lesser degree all the northern coast of Spain, and even the coast of France. The <i>Prestige</i> finally split and sank.
</p><p>Zapatero blamed the Government's handling of the events during and after the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main point of friction between Aznar and Zapatero, however, was the war in Iraq. Opinion polls showed that a clear majority of Spanish voters (around 90%) were against the U.S.-led attack against <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a>'s regime.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Among them, Zapatero who considered any action against Saddam's regime to be illegal and was opposed to the very concept of <a href="/wiki/Preemptive_war" title="Preemptive war">preemptive war</a>.
</p><p>On 26 May 2003 a <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-42" title="Yakovlev Yak-42">Yakovlev Yak-42</a> plane carrying Spanish soldiers home from <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> crashed in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. The plane had been hired by an agency of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. Zapatero blamed Aznar and his government for neglecting aspects like the plane insurance or safety. Further, Aznar had rejected calls for a full inquiry into the crash.<sup id="cite_ref-wsws_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsws-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> After the 2004 March elections it was proven that there had been serious irregularities in the identification of the corpses resulting in a high number of mistakes.<sup id="cite_ref-wsws_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsws-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Concerning the <a href="/wiki/European_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="European Constitution">European Constitution</a>, Zapatero criticized the People's Party Government for fighting to preserve the distribution of power agreed by the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nice" title="Treaty of Nice">Treaty of Nice</a> in the new Constitution. Zapatero thought that Spain should accept a lesser share of power.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2003_local_elections">2003 local elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2003 local elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="box-BLP_sources_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section of a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">biography of a living person</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living persons that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>, especially if potentially <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Libel" title="Wikipedia:Libel">libelous</a> or harmful.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">"José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2009</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On 25 May 2003, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=May_2003_Madrid_Assembly_election&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="May 2003 Madrid Assembly election (page does not exist)">first local and regional elections</a> since Zapatero's appointment as leader of the Socialist party were held. The Socialist Party received a larger popular vote (which prompted Zapatero to claim his party had been the winner) but the People's Party obtained more posts in councils and regional governments. In general, there were not many changes in the results compared to those of the previous Elections held in 1999. The Socialists lost the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> but got enough votes in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> to govern through a coalition with the communists of the <a href="/wiki/United_Left_(Spain)" title="United Left (Spain)">United Left</a>. The "victory" was welcomed by Zapatero, as the winner in Madrid had always won the next general election. However, an unexpected scandal, the so-called Madrid Assembly Scandal, negatively affected the socialist expectations of a victory in 2004.
</p><p>After the Madrid election, the People's Party lacked two seats to obtain an absolute majority. This seemed to allow an alliance of Socialists and the United Left to seize power. But an unexpected event happened. Eduardo Tamayo and María Teresa Sáez, two Socialist Assembly Members (AMs) angry at the distribution of power in the future regional government between the United Left and the Socialist Party, started a crisis that led to a re-run of the Election in Madrid in October 2003 with the subsequent victory of the People's Party.
</p><p>Zapatero did not accept the account of the Socialist AMs and tried to explain it as a conspiratorial plot caused by speculative interests of the house building industry that would have bribed the AMs to prevent a left-wing government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The People's Party, on the other hand, defended the theory that the anger of the two Socialist AMs was caused by Zapatero's broken promise about the referred distribution of power within the Madrid section of the Socialist Party. That promise would have been made some months before the crisis in exchange of support for one of his more immediate collaborators (<a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Trinidad Jiménez">Trinidad Jiménez</a>), who wanted to become the Socialist candidate for mayor of Madrid (the Spanish capital).
</p><p>Zapatero's team had entered into contact with José Luis Balbás through Enrique Martínez and <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_Caldera" title="Jesús Caldera">Jesús Caldera</a> (then Minister of Labor)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In April 2000, Zapatero, Caldera and José Blanco had had lunch with Eduardo Tamayo in a restaurant in Madrid. Tamayo would later become a representative of Zapatero in the 35th party national conference. At the end of the month "Renovadores de la Base" (the faction of Tamayo and Balbás) decided to support Zapatero and the later agreed to be part of Zapatero's team.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He played an important role during Zapatero's promotion. For example, Balbás together with <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Blanco_L%C3%B3pez" title="José Blanco López">José Blanco</a> controlled the list of delegates.
</p><p>During the Debate over the State of the Nation, an annual debate that takes place in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Congress_of_Deputies" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Congress of Deputies">Spanish Congress of Deputies</a>, Zapatero was harshly criticised by José María Aznar on account of the scandal. For the first time, the opinion polls showed that most Spaniards believed that the then Spanish Prime Minister had been the winner (Zapatero had always been considered the winner since his first debate in 2001).
</p><p>Later, in October, a regional election took place in Catalonia, whose results were worse than expected for the Socialist Party. As most of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">Autonomous communities of Spain</a> hold the elections to their assemblies the same day, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, Catalonia, <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, coinciding with the municipal elections all over Spain, the results are hugely significant.
</p><p>On 16 November 2003, the regional election for the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Catalonia" title="Parliament of Catalonia">Assembly of Catalonia</a> was held. Two days before, Zapatero had predicted a historic victory for the <a href="/wiki/Socialists%27_Party_of_Catalonia" title="Socialists&#39; Party of Catalonia">Socialists' Party of Catalonia</a> and the beginning of the People's Party defeat. The Socialist Party won the election in popular vote but CiU obtained more MPs due to the electoral law. The final results were 46 seats for <a href="/wiki/Convergence_and_Union" title="Convergence and Union">Convergence and Union</a> (CiU) (ten fewer than in 1999, the year of the previous election), 42 for the Socialist Party (ten fewer), 15 for the People's Party (three more), 9 for <a href="/wiki/Iniciativa_per_Catalunya-Verds" class="mw-redirect" title="Iniciativa per Catalunya-Verds">Iniciativa per Catalunya-Verds</a> and 23 (nine more) for the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Left_of_Catalonia" title="Republican Left of Catalonia">Republican Left of Catalonia</a>. Zapatero attributed the bad results to the consequences of the crisis of Madrid. However, Maragall became the President of the Regional Government after a Pact with Republican Left of Catalonia and Iniciativa per Catalunya-Verds.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>That alliance resulted in another setback for the Socialist Party when the Spanish newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Diario_ABC" class="mw-redirect" title="Diario ABC">ABC</a></i> published an article stating that Josep-Lluís <a href="/wiki/Carod-Rovira" class="mw-redirect" title="Carod-Rovira">Carod-Rovira</a>, leader of Republican Left of Catalonia, had met some <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a> members secretly in January 2004. According to <i>ABC</i>, Carod-Rovira had promised to provide ETA with political support if the group did not act in Catalonia, which seemed to have been confirmed by the ETA announcement of a truce affecting only that region some months later, before the general election of 2004. Carod-Rovira resigned as vice president of the Catalan government, but continued to be the leader of his party. The scandal damaged Zapatero's image, as ETA and political violence are controversial issues in Spain and Carod-Rovira's party was seen as a possible ally if Zapatero won the election.
</p><p>At end of 2003 and the beginning of 2004 the Spanish political parties started to prepare themselves for the <a href="/wiki/2004_Spanish_legislative_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Spanish legislative election">general election of 2004</a>. All of the opinion polls elaborated at the time foreseen a defeat for Zapatero, as they always predicted a new victory for the People's Party.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_2004_general_election">The 2004 general election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The 2004 general election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_campaign">Election campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Election campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The campaign for the General Election started a fortnight before 14 March 2004. Polls favoured the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party</a>, with some polls predicting a possible repeat of their absolute majority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Previously, on 8 January 2004, Zapatero had created a Committee of Notables composed of 10 highly qualified experts with  considerable political weight. Its mission was to help him to become prime minister. Among its members: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bono" class="mw-redirect" title="José Bono">José Bono</a> (his ex-rival for the Secretaryship of the party and later appointed Minister of Defence), <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Ibarra" title="Juan Carlos Rodríguez Ibarra">Juan Carlos Rodríguez Ibarra</a> (president of the regional government of <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> and one of the most important socialist leaders), <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Moratinos" title="Miguel Ángel Moratinos">Miguel Ángel Moratinos</a> (his minister of foreign affairs 2004–2010), <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Peces-Barba" title="Gregorio Peces-Barba">Gregorio Peces-Barba</a> (later appointed by him High Commissioner for the Victims of Terrorism, although he has already made public his resignation), <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Calvo" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmen Calvo">Carmen Calvo</a> (later appointed minister of culture), etc.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ten days later, on 18 January 2004, Zapatero announced that he would only become prime minister if the Spanish Socialist Workers Party received a plurality, renouncing possible parliamentary alliances in advance if that situation did not happen after the election. Minority parties (especially <a href="/wiki/United_Left_(Spain)" title="United Left (Spain)">United Left</a>, a communist party) criticized the decision, for they considered it an attempt to attract their own voters, who would rather ensure a defeat of the People's Party even at the expense of voting for an unfavorable party.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero's slogan became "we deserve a better Spain", which was coupled with "Zapatero Presidente", or "(ZP)", which became a popular nickname of the then Spanish Prime Minister.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_promises">Campaign promises</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Campaign promises">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>180,000 new houses every year to buy or to rent</li>
<li>Preservation of a balanced budget with no deficit but with a more flexible approach than that of the People's Party</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bilingual_education" title="Bilingual education">Bilingual education</a> (English and Spanish, together with the official regional language in the areas where it existed)</li>
<li>A computer for every two students</li>
<li>A two-year maximum for legal processes or financial compensation</li>
<li>Further investment in research and development</li>
<li>Make the <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Televisión Española">state-owned television company</a> more independent from the government by making its director answerable to parliament, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-#answer_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-#answer-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>During the campaign, Zapatero harshly criticized the People's Party for its management of the <i><a href="/wiki/Prestige_oil_spill" title="Prestige oil spill">Prestige</a></i> crisis, its attitude towards the invasion of <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and the high cost of housing. <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a>, the new leader of the People's Party after <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">Aznar's</a> voluntary retirement, on his part, attacked Zapatero's foreseeable future alliances with parties like United Left or Republican Left of Catalonia (a pro-Independence Catalan party).
</p><p>One of the most important points of friction was the absence of televised debates between the candidates. Zapatero was the first to propose a debate to Mariano Rajoy. Rajoy accepted on the condition that Zapatero could not be alone but accompanied at least by two of his potential allies after the election: <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Llamazares" title="Gaspar Llamazares">Gaspar Llamazares</a> (the leader of United Left) and <a href="/wiki/Josep-Llu%C3%ADs_Carod-Rovira" title="Josep-Lluís Carod-Rovira">Josep-Lluís Carod-Rovira</a> (leader of <a href="/wiki/Republican_Left_of_Catalonia" title="Republican Left of Catalonia">Republican Left of Catalonia</a>). Rajoy justified his decision on the grounds that, in his opinion, he was not running against the Socialist Party but against a "coalition" of forces opposed to the People's Party's policies. Zapatero never formally responded to this proposal and throughout the campaign he continued criticizing what he always defined as Rajoy's reluctance to defend his political program face-to-face. (Zapatero has promised to change electoral law to make televised debates compulsory.)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Madrid_bombings">Madrid bombings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Madrid bombings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 11 March 2004 the most deadly peacetime <a href="/wiki/11_March_2004_Madrid_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="11 March 2004 Madrid attacks">attacks</a> in Spanish history took place. Several commuter trains were bombed, causing 191 deaths and outrage all over Spain. The attacks took place three days before the General Election and all electoral activities were suspended. The common sorrow, instead of promoting unity among Spaniards, increased the already bitter tone of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The People's Party government and Zapatero (who accused ETA in a radio statement broadcast at 8:50&#160;am), initially claimed the attacks to be the work of ETA, an armed <a href="/wiki/Basque_nationalism" title="Basque nationalism">Basque nationalist</a> separatist organization. Later, after an audiotape in <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> was found in a van near a railway station where the perpetrators boarded one of the trains, Aznar declared that all of the possibilities were being investigated.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The government was accused of manipulating information about who was responsible for the attacks to avoid the consequences of public anger at a bombing motivated by its foreign policy – Aznar personally phoned the editors of the four national daily newspapers to tell them that ETA were responsible, whilst Minister of the Interior <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Acebes" title="Ángel Acebes">Ángel Acebes</a> attacked those who believed that responsibility lay elsewhere, despite not offering any evidence for ETA's culpability,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and the state broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Televisión Española">TVE</a> initially failed to report the protest outside the Popular Party's headquarters which ran through the night before the day of the election.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero himself has repeatedly accused the Popular Party of lying about those who were responsible for the attacks. On the other hand, the book <i>11-M. La venganza</i> by Casimiro Abadillo, a Spanish journalist who works for the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)">El Mundo</a></i>, claims that, before the General Election, Zapatero had told that newspaper's director, Pedro J. Ramirez, that two <a href="/wiki/Suicide_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicide bombing">suicide bombers</a> had been found among the victims (although the specialists that examined the bodies said they found no such evidence).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> When he was asked in December 2004 about the issue by the Parliamentary Investigative Committee created to find the truth about the attacks, he declared that he did not remember what he had said.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_day">Election day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Election day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The campaign had ended abruptly two days before it was expected to convene as a result of the bombings. The day before the elections – in this case 13 March 2004 – is considered to be a "Day of Reflection" under Spanish electoral law, with candidates and their parties legally barred from political campaigning. Despite this prohibition, numerous demonstrations took place against the government of José María Aznar in front of the premises of the People's Party all over Spain. There were some claims that most of these demonstrations were instigated or orchestrated by the Socialist Party, through the use of SMS text messaging from mobile phones belonging to the Socialist Party. The Socialist Party publicly denied these accusations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>As the demonstrations escalated, Mariano Rajoy himself appeared on national TV to denounce the illegal demonstrations. In reply, both José Blanco and Alfredo Pérez Rubalcaba broke the silence from the Socialist Party's side, in separate appearances. In the end both sides accused each other of breaking the electoral law on reflection day.
</p><p>In this climate of social unrest and post-attack shock, the <a href="/wiki/2004_Spanish_general_election" title="2004 Spanish general election">elections</a> were held on 14 March 2004. Zapatero's Socialist Party won the elections, with 164 seats in the Cortes, while the People's Party obtained 148. It seems likely that the election result was influenced to a greater or lesser extent by the Spanish public's response to the attacks<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and the informative coverage by the different media and political parties. He took office on 17 April.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_of_the_attacks_on_the_election_outcome">Influence of the attacks on the election outcome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Influence of the attacks on the election outcome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An important point of controversy is if the purpose of the Madrid attacks were to force a Socialist victory; at issue as well was that, if that was the case, whether they succeeded in altering the final result. This has been called the "4 March theory" (that is, if the election had been scheduled for 7 March, the attacks would have taken place on 4 March) by Aznar, among others. No definitive data exists in favour of that possibility but some facts have been used to support it. Thus, the first question Jamal Zougam (one of the first arrested suspects) made when he arrived at the Courthouse on 15 March 2004 was: 'Who won the election?'.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>How the bombing influenced the results is widely debated. The three schools of thought are:
</p>
<ul><li>The attacks themselves might have changed the electoral winner. A sufficient number of voters suddenly decided to vote for the Socialist party because they thought that if it won, Islamist terrorism would be placated.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>The handling of the attacks by the government, rather than the attacks themselves, might have changed the electoral winner. People who had the perception that the information about the attacks was being manipulated decided to vote the Socialist party as a response.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>The attacks might have changed the result but not the winner. The Socialist Party was going to win but with fewer votes. (Despite this claim, most polls before the attacks gave a victory to <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a>.)</li></ul>
<p>The theory that the bombing affected the result is a <a href="/wiki/Counterfactual_conditional" title="Counterfactual conditional">counterfactual</a> that cannot be verified. As elections in European states hinge on social and economic policies mainly, it is equally possible the terrorist events had no notable effect. In this regard, a majority of 74%<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> of the Spanish people were against Spanish involvement in the war.
</p><p>On 13 June 2004 (three months after the General Election) the Election for the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> took place. The Socialist Party tied with 25 seats vs 25 for the People's Party (out of 54), but narrowly won in popular vote. Although <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Borrell" class="mw-redirect" title="José Borrell">José Borrell</a> was the official candidate, Zapatero played an important role in that campaign (as is usual in Spain).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Premiership">Premiership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Premiership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-weight: normal; background-color: #DEDEDE;"><span style="font-size:80%">Styles of</span><br /><b><span class="fn">José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</span></b></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="Spanish Presidential Flag.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg/50px-Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg/75px-Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg/100px-Spanish_Presidential_Flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2071" data-file-height="2071" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">Reference style</a></th><td><i>Excelentísimo Señor (Don)</i></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Spoken style</th><td><i>Señor Presidente</i></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Alternative style</th><td><i>Señor</i> Zapatero, <i><a href="/wiki/Don_(honorific)" title="Don (honorific)">Don</a></i> José Luis</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>His style's defining word is <i>(buen) talante</i>, roughly "pleasantness", "niceness" or "good disposition", which is in brisk and carefully chosen contrast with the more confrontational and brusque premiership style of previous Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a>. Similarly, Zapatero has been quoted to shy away from adopting unpopular measures, having a "habit of showering public money on any problem" and, in all, being "averse to tough decisions".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Withdrawal_from_Iraq">Withdrawal from Iraq</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Withdrawal from Iraq">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the first measures he carried out as soon as he took office was to withdraw every Spanish soldier fighting in Iraq, calling the invasion of that country "an error based on lies".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In less than a month, his nation's 1,300 troops were withdrawn from Iraq. This drew criticism from the right, who held the view that he was ceding to the pressure of the terrorists who attacked Spain. However, it was a measure announced by him before the general elections and supported by the majority of Spanish population.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_policy">Domestic policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Domestic policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
