<p>Much of Zapatero's work has been on social issues, including <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a>-motivated violence and discrimination,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> divorce<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The most recent social issue tackled has been the Dependency Law,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> a plan to regulate help and resources for people in dire need of them, and who cannot provide for themselves and must rely on others on a daily basis. Zapatero has also made it clear that he values funding of research and development and higher education and believes them to be essential for Spain's economic competitiveness. At the same time, he increased the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> and pursued other socialist policies. Scholarships were made available to all, and young adults received rent subsidies called “emancipation” money. The elderly got stipends for nursing care, mothers got $3,500 for the birth of a child, and toddlers attended free nurseries.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Legislation against domestic abuse was introduced, together with a law under which people who are dependent (for reasons such as having a disability) are entitled to a state pension. To safeguard  dependents, a board was established that estimates for each person based on their disability what they are entitled to, as a right. Equally, people required to stay at home to look after the disabled are entitled to a dependency salary. In regards to migrants, 700,000 were granted amnesty in the first year of the Zapatero Government. Steps were also taken to address the vulnerability of people on temporary work contracts, making it more difficult for employers to fire at will and easier for workers to get mortgages.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_problems">Economic problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economic problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Facing a recession and rising unemployment, Zapatero pledged to cut government spending by 4.5% and raise taxes, but not income taxes.  The Popular Party contended that Zapatero lacked a coherent economic plan and stated "There is no tax increase capable of filling the hole that you have created". On 23 June 2008 Zapatero announced 21 reforms designed to aid economic recovery in a speech pointedly avoiding popular terms of the period such as 'crisis'.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Although government deficits were projected to increase to 10% of GDP, Zapatero promised to reduce it to 3% required by EU policy by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2011 Spain's Unemployment Rate had risen to 20.33% exceeding his target rate of 19.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: LGBT rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The legalization of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain" title="Same-sex marriage in Spain">same-sex marriage in Spain</a> on 1 July 2005 includes <a href="/wiki/LGBT_adoption" title="LGBT adoption">adoption rights</a> as well as other rights that were previously only available to heterosexual couples. This caused a stir within the Catholic Church,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> which opposed the measures and supported a demonstration attended by some 166,000 (according to official figures) and one million people (according to the organisers) in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Zapatero's government was also responsible for a Gender Identity Law that allows <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> persons the right to have their identity legally recognised, the criteria being one clinical evaluation and two years of treatment (generally hormone replacement therapy), and without demanding mandatory genital surgery or irreversible sterility.  The law is, along with the legislation of some US states, one of the most simple and non-bureaucratic that currently exist in the world.  Transgender persons also have the right to marry persons of the opposite or same sex they have transitioned into, and to biologically parent children either before or after transitioning.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_territorial_tensions">Regional territorial tensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Regional territorial tensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Zapatero has often declared that his government will not be "soft on terrorism" and will not allow regional nationalists to endanger Spanish unity.
</p><p>On 13 November 2003 in a rally in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> during the election campaign that took <a href="/wiki/Pasqual_Maragall" title="Pasqual Maragall">Pasqual Maragall</a> to power in the <a href="/wiki/Generalitat" title="Generalitat">Generalitat</a>, Rodríguez Zapatero gave a famous promise to approve the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Statute of Catalonia">Statute of Catalonia</a>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I will support the reform of the Statute of Catalonia that the Parliament of Catalonia approves.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>In October 2005, a controversial<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> proposal to reform the Catalan statute arrived at the Spanish parliament after being passed in Catalonia. Zapatero, who had often expressed his support for a change of the statute (although he did not entirely support the draft passed by the Catalan Parliament), supported the reform.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Civil_War_remnants">Spanish Civil War remnants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spanish Civil War remnants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2004 Zapatero's government undertook the task of morally and legally rehabilitating those who were suppressed during and after the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, by instituting a Memorial Commission chaired by Vice-Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Teresa_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_la_Vega" title="María Teresa Fernández de la Vega">María Teresa Fernández de la Vega</a>.
</p><p>On 17 March 2005, Zapatero's government ordered the removal of the last remaining statue of former dictator <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> that remained in Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reform_of_the_education_system">Reform of the education system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Reform of the education system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">"José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2009</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg/220px-Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg/330px-Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg/440px-Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zapatero_junto_con_los_nuevos_ministros_del_Gobierno.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Zapatero along with some of the Government, 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>Just after he took office, Zapatero repealed the law reforming the Education System passed by the previous government and, in November 2005, introduced his own reform bill. The bill was opposed by the People's Party, the Catholic Church, the Muslim community, The Catholic Confederation of Parents' Associations and an important part of the educational community, often for disparate reasons. Complaints against the reform include the limits it imposes upon parents' freedom to choose a school, the decrease in academic status of voluntary religious education, the introduction of a compulsory course ("<a href="/wiki/Education_for_Citizenship_(Spain)" title="Education for Citizenship (Spain)">Education for Citizenship</a>") and a perceived ineffectiveness of the reform in terms of combating poor educational results. The last complaint would be reinforced by the opinion that Spain has ranked poorly amongst the developed countries in the quality and results of its education.
</p><p>After a major demonstration took place against this education reform, the government held a series of meetings with many of the organizations that opposed the reform, reaching agreements with some of them (especially parents' associations and teachers' unions). Some others, most prominently the People's Party and the Catholic Church remain staunchly opposed to it.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ETA">ETA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: ETA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ETA%27s_2006_ceasefire_declaration" title="ETA&#39;s 2006 ceasefire declaration">ETA's 2006 ceasefire declaration</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a> declared what it described at the time as a "permanent <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">ceasefire</a>" that began on midnight 23 March 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> On 5 June 2007, ETA declared this ceasefire over.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> After the initial ceasefire declaration, he informed the Congress that steps would be taken to negotiate with them in order to end its terrorist campaign while denying that there would be any political price paid to put an end to ETA.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The PP grew concerned about the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Concession_(politics)" title="Concession (politics)">political concessions</a> being made to the group to stop their ways, and actively opposed anything other than the possibility of an organized surrender and dismantling of ETA, refusing to support any kind of negotiation.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On 30 December 2006 the ceasefire was broken when a car bomb exploded in <a href="/wiki/2006_Madrid_Barajas_International_Airport_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Madrid Barajas International Airport bombing">Madrid's International Airport, Barajas</a> and ETA claimed authorship. Following this, Zapatero gave orders to halt initiatives leading to negotiations with ETA.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Demonstrations across Spain followed the next day, most condemning the attack, others condemning the Government's policies and a minority even questioning the authorship of the Madrid bombings.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A massive rally in Madrid followed on 25 February 2007 promoted by the Victims of Terrorism Association (AVT in Spanish acronym), rejecting what are perceived to be concessions from the government to the separatists.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 March 2007 a new massive rally was held in Madrid gathering -depending on the source's relationships to the government-  between 342,000 and over two million people.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> This demonstration was organized by the opposition party PP and backed by the AVT and several other associations of victims, to not allow <a href="/wiki/I%C3%B1aki_de_Juana_Chaos" title="Iñaki de Juana Chaos">Iñaki de Juana Chaos</a> out of prison and accusing Zapatero's government of surrendering to terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the meeting of the European Union Justice and Home Affairs Ministers held in <a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a> on 22 September 2006, some of the European ministers reprimanded the Spanish authorities for the aforementioned massive regularisation of undocumented immigrants which was regarded as too loose and opposed to the policies of other State members (on 2 September and 3 alone, during the height of the last illegal immigration wave, 2,283 people arrived illegally in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> having shipped from <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> aboard 27 <a href="/wiki/Pirogue" title="Pirogue">pirogues</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy">Foreign policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Foreign policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg/220px-El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg/330px-El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg/440px-El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_presidente_del_Gobierno_asiste_a_la_III_Cumbre_UE_-_%C3%81frica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gaddafi" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaddafi">Gaddafi</a> with Spanish Prime Minister José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero at the third EU-Africa Summit in Tripoli in November 2010.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq">Iraq</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Iraq">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before being elected, Zapatero opposed the American policy in regard to <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> pursued by Prime Minister Aznar. During the electoral campaign Zapatero promised to withdraw the troops if control in Iraq was not passed to the United Nations after 30 June (the ending date of the initial Spanish military agreement with the multinational coalition that had overthrown Saddam Hussein). Zapatero declared that he did not intend to withdraw the Spanish troops before that date after being questioned about the issue by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party's</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a> in his inauguration parliamentary debate as Prime Minister.
</p><p>On 19 April 2004 Zapatero announced the withdrawal of the 1,300 Spanish troops in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The decision aroused international support worldwide, though the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush_administration" class="mw-redirect" title="George W. Bush administration">Bush administration</a> claimed that terrorists could perceive it as "a victory obtained due to the <a href="/wiki/2004_Madrid_train_bombings" title="2004 Madrid train bombings">2004 Madrid train bombings</a>". <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic party</a> candidate for the U.S. Presidency, asked Zapatero not to withdraw the Spanish soldiers. Some months after withdrawing the troops, the Zapatero government agreed to increase the number of Spanish soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and to send troops to <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> to show the Spanish Government's willingness to spend resources on international missions approved by the United Nations.
</p><p>On 8 June 2004, with the withdrawal already complete, Zapatero's government voted in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> in favour of Resolution 1546 where the following could be read:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Security Council, Recognising the importance of international support [...] for the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraqi people">people of Iraq</a> [...], Affirming the importance of international assistance in reconstruction and development of the Iraqi economy [...]
</p><p>15. Requests Member States and international and regional organizations to contribute assistance to the multinational force, including <b>military forces</b>, as agreed with the Government of Iraq, to help meet the needs of the Iraqi people for security and stability, humanitarian and reconstruction assistance, and to support the efforts of UNAMI […]<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-BLP_sources_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section of a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">biography of a living person</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living persons that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>, especially if potentially <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Libel" title="Wikipedia:Libel">libelous</a> or harmful.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">"José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2009</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/%C2%BFPor_qu%C3%A9_no_te_callas%3F" title="¿Por qué no te callas?">¿Por qué no te callas?</a></div>
<p>An important change in Spanish foreign policy was Zapatero's decision to approach left-wing leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Hugo Chávez</a>. Zapatero played an important role in the improvement of the relationship between the Cuban government and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.
</p><p>At the end of March 2005, Zapatero travelled to Venezuela to sign a deal to sell military ships and aircraft to Venezuela worth around US$1 billion. The US government attempted to intervene but failed, accusing Venezuela of being a "dangerous country."
</p><p>After the election of <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> in Bolivia, Spain was one of the countries the new president visited during his first international tour.
</p><p>At the 2007 Ibero–American Summit, Chávez called Zapatero's predecessor <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a> a fascist for allegedly supporting the 2002 coup attempt. Zapatero used his speaking time to defend Aznar, noting that he was "democratically elected by the Spanish people." Chávez kept trying to interrupt Zapatero, even as summit organisers turned off his microphone. <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">King Juan Carlos</a>, who was seated beside Zapatero, attempted to rebuke Chávez, but was stopped by Zapatero who, displaying significant patience, told him to wait a moment. When Chávez continued to interrupt Zapatero, Juan Carlos, in a rare outburst of anger, asked Chávez "<a href="/wiki/%C2%BFPor_qu%C3%A9_no_te_callas%3F" title="¿Por qué no te callas?">¿Por qué no te callas?</a>" (Why don't you shut up?). The king left the hall shortly afterwards when the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nicaragua" title="President of Nicaragua">President of Nicaragua</a> began to criticize the Spanish government as well. Zapatero continued to participate in the negotiations, later delivering, to loud applause, a speech demanding respect for the leaders of other countries.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The relations between Zapatero and former U.S. president <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> were difficult, mostly as a result of Zapatero's opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>.
</p><p>On 12 October 2003, during the <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Nacional_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Fiesta Nacional de España">Fiesta Nacional de España</a> military parade held in Madrid, then <a href="/wiki/Opposition_leader" class="mw-redirect" title="Opposition leader">opposition leader</a> and presidential candidate Zapatero remained seated as a <a href="/wiki/U.S._Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a> honour guard carrying the <a href="/wiki/American_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="American flag">American flag</a> walked past Zapatero and other VIPs. Everybody else stood as with the rest of the foreign guest armies representations.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> He declared afterwards that his action was a protest against the war and certainly not intended as an insult to the American people.
</p><p>Later on, during an official visit to Tunisia shortly after Zapatero was elected, he asked all of the countries with troops in Iraq to withdraw their soldiers. This declaration moved Bush to send a letter expressing discontent to the Spanish premier.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>American troops were subsequently instructed to not take part during the traditional military parade on the Spanish national holiday in 2004 and in 2005, something which they used to, as both the Spanish and American armies –being <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> allies– are part of joint humanitarian missions; American troops returned to the military parade in 2006; this time Zapatero, being the Spanish premier, stood.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero publicly stated his support for <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> as a candidate running in the <a href="/wiki/2004_United_States_presidential_election" title="2004 United States presidential election">U.S. Presidential election in 2004</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> After the election took place, winner George W. Bush did not return Zapatero's congratulation phone call, though the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> firmly denied that Bush's intention was to snub the Spanish prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, Zapatero repeatedly insisted that Spain's relations with the United States were good. In spite of that, Zapatero acknowledged years after that the phone conversation held with President George W. Bush was "unforgettable" and that when told that the Spanish troops were leaving Iraq, the American president had told him "I am very disappointed in you" and that the conversation ended in a "very cold" manner.<sup id="cite_ref-hastalavista_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hastalavista-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero later told a <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> reporter off the record that he had a "certain consideration" for Bush, because "I recognise that my electoral success has been influenced by his governing style", i.e., that Bush was so unpopular in Spain that he helped Zapatero win in 2004 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-hastalavista_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hastalavista-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2009, Spain announced that it would withdraw its forces from <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">Kosovo</a>. <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">US State Department</a> spokesman Robert Wood issued unusually strong criticism by stating that the United States was "deeply disappointed" by the decision. He said that Washington only learned of the move shortly before Spain announced it publicly. Spanish Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Carme_Chacon" class="mw-redirect" title="Carme Chacon">Carme Chacon</a> made the announcement saying, "The mission has been completed and it is time to return home." Asked if the United States shared that assessment, Wood said, "Not at all."<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Later on, Vice President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> stated that the American relationship with Spain goes beyond "whatever disagreement we may have over Kosovo".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">"José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2009</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Zapatero's predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a>, defended a strong <a href="/wiki/Atlanticist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlanticist">Atlanticist</a> policy. Zapatero has downplayed that policy in favour of a <a href="/wiki/Pro-Europeanism" title="Pro-Europeanism">pan-European</a> one. He has also sponsored the idea of an <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Civilizations" title="Alliance of Civilizations">Alliance of Civilizations</a> which is co-sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Turkey" title="Prime Minister of Turkey">Turkish Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a>.
</p><p>In the writing of what was to be the <a href="/wiki/European_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="European Constitution">European Constitution</a> Zapatero accepted the distribution of power proposed by countries such as Germany and France. After signing the treaty in Rome together with other leaders, he decided to call for a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>, which was held on 20 February 2005. It was the first referendum on the EU treaty, a fact highly publicized by Zapatero's government. A 'Yes' vote was supported by the Socialist Party and the People's Party and as a result almost 77% voted in favour of the European Constitution, but turnout was around 43%. However, this result came to nothing when a referendum in France voted to reject the European Constitution which meant that the EU could not ratify the treaty because support was not unanimous.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Presidency of the Council of the European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 1 January 2010, Spain assumed the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> for the first six months of the 18-month 'Trio' along with <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>. The development of the Stockholm Programme Action Plan, the impulse for the EU adhesion to the European Convention on Human Rights, the setting up of the new plan for effective equality between women and men, and the political decision to promote the European protection order, were all important advances achieved under the Spanish Presidency.
</p><p>Within days, Spain's web site for its Presidency www.eu2010.es was defaced by a picture of the main character of a popular television show, <a href="/wiki/Mr._Bean" title="Mr. Bean">Mr. Bean</a>, the supposed lookalike of Zapatero<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> although the <a href="/wiki/Cross-site_scripting" title="Cross-site scripting">XSS</a> attack lasted only several hours.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France_and_Germany">France and Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: France and Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 March 2005, Zapatero became the first Spanish prime minister to speak to the French National Assembly. He supported the PS candidate <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9gol%C3%A8ne_Royal" title="Ségolène Royal">Ségolène Royal</a> during her campaign for the <a href="/wiki/2007_French_presidential_election" title="2007 French presidential election">2007 French presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Zapatero directly supported the SPD candidate, Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Gerhard Schröder">Gerhard Schröder</a>, before the <a href="/wiki/2005_German_federal_election" title="2005 German federal election">German election of 18 September 2005</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Gibraltar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">"José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Jos%C3%A9+Luis+Rodr%C3%ADguez+Zapatero%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2009</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>While Zapatero complained about <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>'s celebrations for the tricentenary of British rule and rejected the Gibraltarians' requests for Spain to recognise their right to self-determination, at the end of 2004 his policy changed and he became the first Spanish prime minister to accept the participation of Gibraltar as a partner on the same level as Spain and the United Kingdom in discussions both countries hold regularly concerning the territory. The decision was criticized by many in Spain as a surrender of their claim to sovereignty over Gibraltar as well as an alleged disruption of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>. Zapatero said it was a new way to solve a 300-year-old issue.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2006_Franco%E2%80%93Italian%E2%80%93Spanish_Middle_East_Peace_Plan" title="2006 Franco–Italian–Spanish Middle East Peace Plan">2006 Franco–Italian–Spanish Middle East Peace Plan</a></div>
<p>Zapatero condemned the <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 Lebanon War</a>. Zapatero issued a statement saying that "From my point of view, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> is wrong. One thing is self defense, and the other is to launch a counter offensive consisting on a general attack in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_strip" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaza strip">Gaza</a> that is just going to further escalate violence in the area".<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_election">2008 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 2008 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_general_election,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish general election, 2008">Spanish general election, 2008</a></div>
<p>On 9 March 2008, Zapatero's <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a> (PSOE) won the general election with 44% of the votes.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Two days earlier, on 7 March, <a href="/wiki/Isa%C3%ADas_Carrasco" title="Isaías Carrasco">Isaías Carrasco</a>, a PSOE <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque</a> politician was shot dead in what is believed to be an attack by <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a>, and which resulted in the agreed canceling of the final days of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Premiership">Post-Premiership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Post-Premiership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>He left office on 20 December 2011<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and left the PSOE's Secretary General chair on 4 February 2012 to <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_P%C3%A9rez_Rubalcaba" title="Alfredo Pérez Rubalcaba">Alfredo Pérez Rubalcaba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> On 9 February he entered the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Council_of_State" title="Spanish Council of State">Spanish Council of State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> He was also named President of the Advisory Board of the Institute for Cultural Diplomacy,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> a Berlin-based organization.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
